<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_99267db4-f733-418e-b097-ddb7b445411e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<a href="/questions/1570599-my-almost-8-year-old-just-started-reading">My almost 8 year old just started reading this book on his own. I was unaware that it was part of a series. Will this book make sense to him on its own without having read the first one? (I haven&#39;t read this book or series--my husband pulled it out for him last night when my son asked to read a book about &quot;battle.&quot;)</a>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I did the same thing when I was about the same age. I remember being thrilled to learn there was more! It can be a pretty heavy series though. Many ha<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I did the same thing when I was about the same age. I remember being thrilled to learn there was more! It can be a pretty heavy series though. Many have compared it to The Chronicles of Narnia, but it's very different. Obviously you guys know your son best and whether or not he's up for this series, but it does have some very sad moments in it.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1402324'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F24784.The_Black_Cauldron">like</a></span>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/28837869-melissa"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1496704391i/28837869._UX100_CR0,16,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/28837869-melissa">Melissa</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The Disney movie takes elements from both this book and the first in the series, "The Book of Three", though this is the book it takes it's name from.<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The Disney movie takes elements from both this book and the first in the series, "The Book of Three", though this is the book it takes it's name from. If you're looking to read the book the movie is based on, you're best starting off with The Book of Three.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3256394715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12988716428401345860">Reading this book was like eating a big bowl of ice cream. Its innocent chivalry and intrepid heroism bear the signature of a genius Fantasy writer.<br/><br/>I thought about the Cauldron long and hard. The reasoning by which the characters travel is childish and not really reasonable. But the story is so good.<br/><br/>The other 4 books in the series are ordinary. This one, is not. I really want to reread it again. Don't we all wish that Disney had stuck to the original book? This too applies. Sigh. At least I'm no</span>
  <span id="freeText12988716428401345860" style="display:none">Reading this book was like eating a big bowl of ice cream. Its innocent chivalry and intrepid heroism bear the signature of a genius Fantasy writer.<br /><br />I thought about the Cauldron long and hard. The reasoning by which the characters travel is childish and not really reasonable. But the story is so good.<br /><br />The other 4 books in the series are ordinary. This one, is not. I really want to reread it again. Don't we all wish that Disney had stuck to the original book? This too applies. Sigh. At least I'm not lactose intolerant to great stories.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3056976568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12825524972045009878">A slight retread of book 1, but with a sharper driving quest, higher stakes, and bigger character moments for almost everyone. Except for the looming shadow of the big bad villain, the smaller villains are far more nuanced and morally interesting.<br/><br/>There are more of the lovely thoughtful moments that I prize, where people have to consider the price of heroism and reflect on what makes for a good life. <br/><br/>Looking forward to the next book.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2955606628" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2955606628" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2955606628?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440906490" href="/book/show/1269433.The_Black_Cauldron">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=witch">witch</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2955606628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7866496445333296514">I loved this book. It's definitely the kind of fantasy novel that anybody can enjoy, simple without being dry or boring, sentimental without being saccharine, and it has lots of likeable characters. It does differ from its Disney film adaptation counterpart, and it's actually not the first in its series (although arguably it's the most well-known book of that series), and that makes it really fun to read, because so much of it is unexpected. It's not a particularly deep work of fiction, but its </span>
  <span id="freeText7866496445333296514" style="display:none">I loved this book. It's definitely the kind of fantasy novel that anybody can enjoy, simple without being dry or boring, sentimental without being saccharine, and it has lots of likeable characters. It does differ from its Disney film adaptation counterpart, and it's actually not the first in its series (although arguably it's the most well-known book of that series), and that makes it really fun to read, because so much of it is unexpected. It's not a particularly deep work of fiction, but its universal themes of friendship and adventure really make it stand out. It even has some elements of spookiness, giving it a darker edge than some other similar books in its genre.<br /><br />I loved the developed world in the story, and how the characters and their abilities all compliment each other. No character is just thrown in at random for filler, and they all rely on each other to succeed. It's a very character-driven story, really. It also breaks some of the more common and overused tropes in the fantasy genre, which was great to see.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7866496445333296514" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_955919727" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/955919727" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597876967p2/1343864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/955919727?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780881030938" href="/book/show/295493.The_Black_Cauldron">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=heroes-and-villains">heroes-and-villains</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=kid-lit">kid-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=treasure-and-adventure">treasure-and-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=books-i-missed-during-childhood">books-i-missed-during-childhood</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer955919727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14208883604465749164">This book is the one that gave the Disney film from the 80s its name--you know, the one nobody saw that was a complete box office disaster--right before <i>The Little Mermaid</i> came out and ushered in Disney's Golden Age. I saw the film once and wasn't impressed with it. It bears almost no resemblance, aside from its characters sharing the same names and a few select characteristics, to the books.<br/><br/>As stated in my review for <i>The Book of Three</i>, I was not very impressed with this series to start off with</span>
  <span id="freeText14208883604465749164" style="display:none">This book is the one that gave the Disney film from the 80s its name--you know, the one nobody saw that was a complete box office disaster--right before <i>The Little Mermaid</i> came out and ushered in Disney's Golden Age. I saw the film once and wasn't impressed with it. It bears almost no resemblance, aside from its characters sharing the same names and a few select characteristics, to the books.<br /><br />As stated in my review for <i>The Book of Three</i>, I was not very impressed with this series to start off with, but about a third of the way in to <i>The Black Cauldron</i>, it became clear that Alexander had turned his storytelling around a little. Instead of focusing on plot movement and having things happen to the characters all the time, <i>The Black Cauldron</i> is instead a very character-motivated story. Most of the conflict doesn't come from fighting bad guys, but instead from the difficult choices the characters must make.<br /><br />Although, yes, there is a plot. Taran and his friends join the massive effort to retake the titular Black Cauldron from Arawn, Death Lord of Annuven, so that he may not make any more of his Cauldron Born warriors (basically magical deathless zombies). Only one problem: when they get to Annuven, the Cauldron has already been stolen, so the companions set off again in search of it, to prevent Arawn from making more Cauldron Born, so that when the final inevitable confrontation that is sure to come does occur, they may at least have a chance in defeating him. This search leads Taran to the the three enchantresses in the Marshes of Morva, Orddu, Orgach, and Orwen. They are honestly delightful (a great example of Alexander's skill at combining humor and actual pathos) and more importantly, they pose Taran his greatest challenge yet. Taran, who wants to be a hero, but doesn't actually know what that means.<br /><br />This was probably my favorite of the five books, mostly because the enchantresses were so sassy, but also probably because it was such an unexpected improvement over its predecessor.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14208883604465749164" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bryce Wilson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bryce Wilson" href="/user/show/605328-bryce-wilson">Bryce Wilson</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/605328-bryce-wilson?shelf=ya">ya</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16640669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2261166194178018225">Old Shit I'm Revisiting: The Prequel: Part 2<br/><br/>Aw this is more like it. As I said I was a bit disappointed reading The Book Of Three this is more like The Prydain I remember. There are still flaws, writing at times can be a bit flat, and the exposition a bit heavy. But the moral universe of the characters has grown nicely adding shades of grey to what was starkly black and white before, there's room for some apt and surprisingly lovely metaphor (The broach that causes everything to look different i</span>
  <span id="freeText2261166194178018225" style="display:none">Old Shit I'm Revisiting: The Prequel: Part 2<br /><br />Aw this is more like it. As I said I was a bit disappointed reading The Book Of Three this is more like The Prydain I remember. There are still flaws, writing at times can be a bit flat, and the exposition a bit heavy. But the moral universe of the characters has grown nicely adding shades of grey to what was starkly black and white before, there's room for some apt and surprisingly lovely metaphor (The broach that causes everything to look different is as good a metaphor for loss of innocence as I can think of) and the characters have deepened, though I can still see a bit of the stockness. (blah blah blah classic archetypes yada yada yada collective unconscious, what I can I say I calls them like I see them).<br /><br />Once again though the heart of the book comes from Alexander's fertile and surprisingly dark imagination. He plays for keeps and he can play mean, the Cauldron Born themselves are a skin crawlingly creepy concept (It's always bothered me how they don't even bleed), The Huntsmen blew my God Damned mind when I was twelve, and the Cauldron itself is creepy as hell. It's a clever idea really, Tolkien always did the thing with the ring where it would purposely hinder transportation or put itself in someone's hand. Well that all well and good, but Alexander does the same thing here with a several hundred pound cauldron, which believe me can do some damage when it doesn't want to be moved. Even the allies are creepy as hell, the three sisters who control the cauldron have the same strange elliptical menace as Gaiman's Kindly Ones from Sandman. In fact I wouldn't be at all surprised to learn that this was a major influence on Gaiman's portrayal. (blah blah blah classic archetypes yada yada yada collective unconscious, what I can I say I calls them like I see them).<br /><br />Anyway it was a significant step up from The Book Of Three. I might see some cracks a bit more clearly now, but I can still appreciate a ripping good yarn. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2261166194178018225" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63161822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2873491081671037897">Book 2 of the Chronicles of Prydain series, which I sort of worshipped as a kid. I really wish that my copy of the book features the cover pictured with this review, as it seems to ignore Taran completely and just features Eilonwy doing something badass, which is pretty cool. <br/><br/>Also, I will repeat a warning I made in my review of <i>The Book of Three</i>: The Walt Disney Corporation, in a well-intended but disasterous move, decided to make an animated movie called The Black Cauldron several years ago. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText2873491081671037897" style="display:none">Book 2 of the Chronicles of Prydain series, which I sort of worshipped as a kid. I really wish that my copy of the book features the cover pictured with this review, as it seems to ignore Taran completely and just features Eilonwy doing something badass, which is pretty cool. <br /><br />Also, I will repeat a warning I made in my review of <i>The Book of Three</i>: The Walt Disney Corporation, in a well-intended but disasterous move, decided to make an animated movie called The Black Cauldron several years ago. The plot is a bastardization of the first two books in the series, and under no circumstances should anyone watch it, ever. Everything is wrong, but what I remember most of all was that they made Eilonwy a fucking <i>blonde</i>. NO. She gets called "Eilonwy of the red-gold hair" at least once in every single book, and the fact that Disney decided to ignore this made me furious when I saw the movie. <br /><br />It may not seem like a big deal, but even as a kid I was always painfully aware of how rare redhaired heroines are. I wanted us to be represented, dammit. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2873491081671037897" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_455199" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/455199" />
    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40533-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271013583p2/40533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/455199?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/40533-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">decent people</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer455199" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15146952638978221739">The first book in the Prydain series didn't exactly impress me. I was afraid the whole lot of them would be stories where this motley crew of adventurers makes one mistake after another because they're silly and self-righteous but somehow manages to magically win in the end.<br/><br/><i>The Black Cauldron</i> changed my mind. While the characters didn't get too much smarter, they matured quite a bit. Their bumbling isn't quite as tiresome, and they seem to learn a lot quicker and think less about themselves. So </span>
  <span id="freeText15146952638978221739" style="display:none">The first book in the Prydain series didn't exactly impress me. I was afraid the whole lot of them would be stories where this motley crew of adventurers makes one mistake after another because they're silly and self-righteous but somehow manages to magically win in the end.<br /><br /><i>The Black Cauldron</i> changed my mind. While the characters didn't get too much smarter, they matured quite a bit. Their bumbling isn't quite as tiresome, and they seem to learn a lot quicker and think less about themselves. So there go all the problems I had with the first book. I finally felt as though these characters deserved to get to the end of their story.<br /><br />But don't worry, Eilonwy is just as snarky, but not quite so obnoxious.<br /><br />Some of Alexander's propensity for coincidences and Deus ex machina remains, but it's not really a fault. It's a style. What he's created in <i>The Black Cauldron</i> is an elegant story about trust, honor, and sacrifice. It's 1,000 times better than <i>The Book of Three</i>, so give it a try. It's easy and light and will take you like 20 seconds to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15146952638978221739" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1492909011" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1492909011" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28801208-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605848284p2/28801208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1492909011?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/28801208-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28403836-the-black-cauldron">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1492909011" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4013711118053527214">I first read all five of Lloyd Alexander's <i>Chronicles of Prydain</i> in my early teens, and frankly, it's hard for me to remember much about them beyond general emotional impressions: the first two were adventurous, the third a bit odd, the fourth dry and philosophical, and the fifth - well, it all went to hell in the fifth book. The announcement of these new yearly 50th Anniversary editions, therefore, are a great excuse not just to revisit the series but to separate them out and consider them some</span>
  <span id="freeText4013711118053527214" style="display:none">I first read all five of Lloyd Alexander's <i>Chronicles of Prydain</i> in my early teens, and frankly, it's hard for me to remember much about them beyond general emotional impressions: the first two were adventurous, the third a bit odd, the fourth dry and philosophical, and the fifth - well, it all went to hell in the fifth book. The announcement of these new yearly 50th Anniversary editions, therefore, are a great excuse not just to revisit the series but to separate them out and consider them somewhat more...individually.<br /><br />The big surprise for me is that in many ways, <i>The Black Cauldron</i> does not feel like its own story. It feels something like an extended coda to <i>The Book of Three</i>. I kept having to think back to the events and characters of the first book, and it seems obvious that Alexander (or his editor) assumed that the eager child reader of 1965 would have read and probably reread that earlier adventure shortly before starting the new one. The first third or so of <i>The Black Cauldron</i> drags a little as we bridge from what happened before, reintroduce familiar friends, and set up an "easy" goal that pretty clearly won't go easily at all.<br /><br />Fortunately, once things start to go wrong for the characters, things start to go very right for the book. The eponymous cauldron (or "Black Crochan") is a golden goose, a total MacGuffin - what it does is ultimately far less important than what it drives people to do. Alexander is examining classical, heroic concepts of pride and honor, along with a more modern treatment of the fine line between light and dark. In Prydain, the greatest heroes still have flaws, and traitors were once good men who should still be remembered for their former, braver deeds. Most intriguing of all are Orddu, Orwen and Orgoch, supernatural figures (implied to be the Three Fates) who are also <i>totally</i> amoral. Their interactions with Taran and his friends are both funny and unsettling in turn. Although Alexander's prose is both straightforward and spare, his gentle contemplations on the complexity of morality are surprisingly effective.<br /><br /><i>The Black Cauldron</i> ends definitively, but the reader is left with the unspoken impression that this is only one small battle in a much bigger war. (Again, it feels like Alexander was writing installments of a series from the outset.) I'm going to be very interested to return next year for <i>The Castle of Llyr</i>; already, we're moving away from simple adventure stories and more into a philosophical examination of Taran's growth. As a child, I found the progression of the series confusing because it defied my "fantasy lit" expectations. As an adult, however, I'm finding it both intriguing and surprisingly rewarding.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4013711118053527214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2229511975" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2229511975" />
    <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos"><img alt="Sotiris Karaiskos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407195235p2/18940246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2229511975?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sotiris Karaiskos" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos">Sotiris Karaiskos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12217099-the-black-cauldron">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2229511975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5775278644289387737">In the second part of this series, the heroes we met in the first are back in action, taking on with the help of a few more warriors a very difficult mission, particularly crucial for the outcome of the fight against evil. As part of this mission, they are confronting great dangers but also themselves and are connected even more through all these difficulties. In the end, however, they find that evil can have many more forms, as well as good, which makes things much more complicated.<br/><br/> These devel</span>
  <span id="freeText5775278644289387737" style="display:none">In the second part of this series, the heroes we met in the first are back in action, taking on with the help of a few more warriors a very difficult mission, particularly crucial for the outcome of the fight against evil. As part of this mission, they are confronting great dangers but also themselves and are connected even more through all these difficulties. In the end, however, they find that evil can have many more forms, as well as good, which makes things much more complicated.<br /><br /> These developments give the author the opportunity to offer us another fascinating adventure that allows also several very emotional moments. There is, of course, again an intense element of humour, as the genre imposes, but the narrative, however, gets a darker mood. Also, there are some clichés in the plot, but I have the impression that the author handles them in a very meaningful way.<br /><br /> So the conclusion is that this book is an ideal continuation of the series, another book that is very difficult to leave it of hands before the last page.<br /><br /><br /> Στο δεύτερο μέρος αυτής της σειράς οι ήρωες που γνωρίσαμε στο πρώτο επιστρέφουν στη δράση αναλαμβάνοντας με τη βοήθεια μερικών ακόμα πολεμιστών μία πολύ δύσκολη αποστολή και ιδιαίτερα κρίσιμη για την έκβαση του αγώνα ενάντια στο κακό. Στα πλαίσια αυτής της αποστολής γνωρίζουν πολύ μεγάλους κινδύνους, έρχονται αντιμέτωποι με τους εαυτούς τους και δένονται ακόμα περισσότερο μέσα από όλες αυτές τις δυσκολίες. Στο τέλος, όμως, διαπιστώνουν ότι το κακό μπορεί να έχει πολύ περισσότερες μορφές, όπως αντιστοίχως και το καλό, κάτι που κάνει τα πράγματα πολύ πιο περίπλοκα.<br /><br /> Αυτές οι εξελίξεις δίνουν στο συγγραφέα τη δυνατότητα να μας προσφέρει άλλη μία συναρπαστική περιπέτεια που η μορφή της επιτρέπει και αρκετές ιδιαίτερα συναισθηματικές στιγμές. Υπάρχει, φυσικά, και πάλι έντονο στοιχείο του χιούμορ, όπως επιβάλλει το είδος, η αφήγηση, όμως, έχει μία πιο σκοτεινή διάθεση. Επίσης δεν λείπουν και κάποια κλισέ στην πλοκή αλλά έχω την εντύπωση ότι ο συγγραφέας ακόμα και αυτά τα χειρίζεται με έναν πολύ ουσιαστικό τρόπο.<br /><br /> Οπότε το συμπέρασμα είναι ότι αυτό το βιβλίο είναι μία ιδανική συνέχεια της σειράς, άλλο ένα βιβλίο το οποίο πολύ δύσκολα αφήνεις από τα χέρια σου πριν την τελευταία σελίδα.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5775278644289387737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1371064736" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1371064736" />
    <a title="Benjamin Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas"><img alt="Benjamin Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451660582p2/4209082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1371064736?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benjamin Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benjamin Thomas" href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas">Benjamin Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4209082-benjamin-thomas?shelf=childrens-books-middle-grade">childrens-books-middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4209082-benjamin-thomas?shelf=fantasy-epic">fantasy-epic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1371064736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16409228407028941222">While I enjoyed the first book in this series, I think part of my enjoyment was due to finally diving into such a classic series that had eluded me for so many years. I did enjoy that first book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24780.The_Book_of_Three__The_Chronicles_of_Prydain___1_' title='The Book of Three (The Chronicles of Prydain, #1) by Lloyd Alexander' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Book of Three</a>, but it did seem to meander a little too much for my taste. This time around, I felt the plot was much tighter and focused on just a handful of characters, allowing me to get to know them much better.<br/><br/>I also liked how Taran, the main character, grew through the novel. He is still an ass</span>
  <span id="freeText16409228407028941222" style="display:none">While I enjoyed the first book in this series, I think part of my enjoyment was due to finally diving into such a classic series that had eluded me for so many years. I did enjoy that first book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24780.The_Book_of_Three__The_Chronicles_of_Prydain___1_" title="The Book of Three (The Chronicles of Prydain, #1) by Lloyd Alexander" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book of Three</a>, but it did seem to meander a little too much for my taste. This time around, I felt the plot was much tighter and focused on just a handful of characters, allowing me to get to know them much better.<br /><br />I also liked how Taran, the main character, grew through the novel. He is still an assistant pig-keeper but he really grows into his leadership role this time around as evidenced by the high impact moral decisions he must make. Not all of the good guys turn out to be so good and the concepts of honor and leadership are paramount. The scenes with the three enchantresses are especially fun to read as they mix humor with danger.<br /><br />Looking forward to the next one, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24779.The_Castle_of_Llyr__The_Chronicles_of_Prydain__3_" title="The Castle of Llyr (The Chronicles of Prydain #3) by Lloyd Alexander" rel="nofollow noopener">The Castle of Llyr</a>.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16626487342250343820">Okay, so I honestly didn't waste much time after finishing the first book because I dove into <i>The Black Cauldron</i> pretty quickly. That being said, I was actually pretty darn excited to dive into this book because I remembered watching the movie when I was little. Heck, I think it's on Disney + right now.<br/><br/>Another honest moment, it has been a very long time since I've seen the film. So at this point, I wasn't even trying to pretend that I remembered what happened in it. I think the girl was like sav</span>
  <span id="freeText16626487342250343820" style="display:none">Okay, so I honestly didn't waste much time after finishing the first book because I dove into <i>The Black Cauldron</i> pretty quickly. That being said, I was actually pretty darn excited to dive into this book because I remembered watching the movie when I was little. Heck, I think it's on Disney + right now.<br /><br />Another honest moment, it has been a very long time since I've seen the film. So at this point, I wasn't even trying to pretend that I remembered what happened in it. I think the girl was like saving herself at one point and the guy was like.. oh can I come? If that's completely wrong and I'm explaining a different movie.. then pretend you didn't see this review.<br /><br />Now after diving in this one.. my view on Taran and Eilonwy has changed a bit. Not sure what exactly happened between the two books but they just got annoying. Like, I clearly remembered that they were kind of cute in the first book when they were together.. but something definitely changed in this one. I don't even think they were that annoying or frustrating to deal with in the movie? <br /><br />Other than that, the adventure was a bit more exciting than the first one. Or at least I was a bit more invested this time around. Probably because this was turned into a movie.. and I have no shame about it at all.<br /><br />In the end, I guess I'm intrigued enough to dive into the next book. I just have to find a version of it to read first.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1114902235" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1114902235" />
    <a title="Dusty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/655483-dusty"><img alt="Dusty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605501426p2/655483.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1114902235?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dusty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dusty" href="/user/show/655483-dusty">Dusty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/6410648-the-black-cauldron">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/655483-dusty?shelf=carly-dusty-book-club">carly-dusty-book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/655483-dusty?shelf=read-before-2007">read-before-2007</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/655483-dusty?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1114902235" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9947701260937279761">My parents bought me the <i>Prydain</i> book series as a bundle, at my insistence, from the Scholastic Book Fair. I was in eighth grade and riding high after a long-awaited family trip to Disneyland. I was also fairly convinced that I wanted to become an animator and had read about Disney's <i>The Black Cauldron</i> (1985) in Bob Thomas's <i>Art of Animation</i>. Since the movie wasn't available on VHS, I figured reading the books upon which it was based was an acceptable alternative. Of course, I did not expect the</span>
  <span id="freeText9947701260937279761" style="display:none">My parents bought me the <i>Prydain</i> book series as a bundle, at my insistence, from the Scholastic Book Fair. I was in eighth grade and riding high after a long-awaited family trip to Disneyland. I was also fairly convinced that I wanted to become an animator and had read about Disney's <i>The Black Cauldron</i> (1985) in Bob Thomas's <i>Art of Animation</i>. Since the movie wasn't available on VHS, I figured reading the books upon which it was based was an acceptable alternative. Of course, I did not expect then to fall in love with Taran, Eilonwy, Gurgi, and the other characters populating Lloyd Alexander's Prydain. I certainly never predicted that I would eventually be able to write -- as I am now writing -- that I have read the series more times (2, going on 3) than I have seen the movie. That although my career dreams have shifted remarkably I remain as attached to the books as I ever was.<br /><br />In <i>The Black Cauldron</i>, Assistant Pig-Keeper Taran follows his thirst for adventure into a dangerous quest against the evil lord Arawn. The book's plot is similar to that of <i>The Book of Three</i>, the first book in the series, in that Taran quickly gets separated from the group, runs into a handful of delightful companions (some new, some old), is saved a time or two by the "fair folk" who live underground, and has to grow up a little along the way. As I stated in my review of <i>The Book of Three</i>, I think my reading of the series is enhanced by the fact that I have read it before and know where it all is headed. Eilonwy's ring, the brooch Taran inherits, the three sorceresses living in the forest -- all these shall return in the books to follow, bringing texture and deeper significance to the relatively small roles they play here. While the books stand alone as decent stories of adventure, I really do think what makes them special is how they join together as a series.<br /><br />A final word about the movie: It is called <i>The Black Cauldron</i>, but it blends events from both <i>The Book of Three</i> and <i>The Black Cauldron</i>. Thus the movie poster, which is on the cover of my edition of the book, includes the Horned King, who actually doesn't appear in the second book at all. There are other differences between the book and movie, including Fflewddue Flam's age and general competence and, of course, the manner by which the titular cauldron is ultimately destroyed. The movie probably deserves its reputation as the worst of Disney's animated movies, and unfortunately the lack of critical and commercial acclaim seems to have led Hollywood to think the series as a whole won't transfer into film. This, I believe, is a terrible misconception. I don't know that I <i>want</i> Prydain on the big screen because that would mean sharing something I have loved having mostly to myself for so many years with the rest of the world, but golly. Such a thoughtful and entertaining series deserves better than Disney gave it back in '85.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9947701260937279761" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2832800216" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5649527789024787202">I liked this a little better than the first in the series, I think. The somewhat bland and bog-standard beginning of the Book of Three no longer applies at all: the story has been untethered and allowed to be its own thing, and continues along its own way in this story. It has the same characters I like from the first, along with a passive-aggressive fairy and a particularly mean-spirited ponce. Pretty much every hero is thrown through the wringer, they all learn and grow as they learned and gre</span>
  <span id="freeText5649527789024787202" style="display:none">I liked this a little better than the first in the series, I think. The somewhat bland and bog-standard beginning of the Book of Three no longer applies at all: the story has been untethered and allowed to be its own thing, and continues along its own way in this story. It has the same characters I like from the first, along with a passive-aggressive fairy and a particularly mean-spirited ponce. Pretty much every hero is thrown through the wringer, they all learn and grow as they learned and grew in the previous, and unlike the last installment, this one also had more than one good twist to it.<br /><br />The prose still quite doesn't catch me, though.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/22886432?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="X" class="user" itemprop="url" name="X" href="/user/show/599861-x">X</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440227434" href="/book/show/1269432.The_Black_Cauldron">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fantasy fans, especially kids  and young adults</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to X by: </span>
      Q
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer22886432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2933869132860195208"> Yet another fast moving, easy reading book. I wish I had read it sooner, as I was confused in the beginning trying to remember who all the characters were. However, after the first chapter or two it was quite good. A few parts were disturbingly LOTR reminiscent, but not enough to make it a cheap rip-off. Most of the characters were good and the mythological influences were nice. I'll think I won't wait so long to read the rest of the series.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1240857956" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1240857956" />
    <a title="Lara Mi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21924792-lara-mi"><img alt="Lara Mi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548829956p2/21924792.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1240857956?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lara Mi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lara Mi" href="/user/show/21924792-lara-mi">Lara Mi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21924792-lara-mi?shelf=6-magic-witches-wizards">6-magic-witches-wizards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21924792-lara-mi?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21924792-lara-mi?shelf=3-fictional-worlds">3-fictional-worlds</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21924792-lara-mi?shelf=5-journeys-adventures">5-journeys-adventures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21924792-lara-mi?shelf=1-fantasy">1-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21924792-lara-mi?shelf=novel-owned">novel-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21924792-lara-mi?shelf=6-royalty">6-royalty</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1240857956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4921029347615396069"><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478992741i/21137652.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>“For each of us comes a time when we must be more than what we are.” <br/>
</blockquote><br/>Taran’s home of Caer Dallben serves as a venue for a great council - Prince Gwydion intends on invading the evil kingdom of Annuvin to seize and destroy their source of power; the black cauldron which spawns deathly warriors. Taran feels honoured to march alongside Gwydion but soon finds himself separated from the company. Luckily, his former companions, the Princess Eilonwy and Gurgi, have followed him in secrecy and are now</span>
  <span id="freeText4921029347615396069" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478992741i/21137652.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>“For each of us comes a time when we must be more than what we are.” <br>
</blockquote><br>Taran’s home of Caer Dallben serves as a venue for a great council - Prince Gwydion intends on invading the evil kingdom of Annuvin to seize and destroy their source of power; the black cauldron which spawns deathly warriors. Taran feels honoured to march alongside Gwydion but soon finds himself separated from the company. Luckily, his former companions, the Princess Eilonwy and Gurgi, have followed him in secrecy and are now ready to help him once again.<br><br><b>The Black Cauldron</b> takes a much darker turn compared to its predecessor. Many new characters are introduced but also several lost. The new characters are all very interesting and I would be glad to see them in later volumes. I still think that this series provides characters who are all quite different from one another despite the short length of the books. <br><br>Taran is still a very likeable main character who is continuously growing. When he acquires a magical brooch that sharpens his senses, his perspective on the world is written in a beautiful manner and generally adds a magical touch to this world. <br><br>Although most things appear very bleak in this second volume, the chapter where the three old crones are introduced is hilarious; they also made an appearance in the Disney adaptation in which I cared little for them. In this original format, however, I find them very likeable and just simply fun to read about – I loved Orgoch’s lip smacking! <br>​<br>As already mentioned, there is also quite a loss of characters. I was surprised to see quite a few deaths so early in the series and I was rather sad about them as they counted among my favoured characters. Somehow, it’s always my favoured characters that die!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4921029347615396069" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1370938420" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1370938420" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7356691-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325898058p2/7356691.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1370938420?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/7356691-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1370938420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14115269215765454518">Me: Okay boys, today we're starting chapter three of the Black Cauldron and-<br/>Student: I FINISHED THE ENTIRE THING AND THE LIBRARY DOESN'T HAVE THE REST SO MY MUM IS GOING TO BUY THEM ALL FOR ME.<br/><br/>I love it when I find things that my reluctant readers get hooked on, and this exchange happened during the second class I've ever had with this kid. I'm all like:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440273895ra/15955508.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Stand back, Mrs. Student'smom, let me work. <br/><br/>So anyway, I read this book when I was a kid and I had basically forgotten how it ended, I just reme</span>
  <span id="freeText14115269215765454518" style="display:none">Me: Okay boys, today we're starting chapter three of the Black Cauldron and-<br>Student: I FINISHED THE ENTIRE THING AND THE LIBRARY DOESN'T HAVE THE REST SO MY MUM IS GOING TO BUY THEM ALL FOR ME.<br><br>I love it when I find things that my reluctant readers get hooked on, and this exchange happened during the second class I've ever had with this kid. I'm all like:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440273895ra/15955508.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Stand back, Mrs. Student'smom, let me work. <br><br>So anyway, I read this book when I was a kid and I had basically forgotten how it ended, I just remember loving it. So I decided to do it with a couple of students and it's going well. When my one kids read it so fast I figured I'd better finish it again quick so I knew what he was talking about when he brought stuff up.<br><br>So far I love using this book to discuss heroism. I think it's also a great book for discussing wisdom; who is wise here? Who would you follow and why? There is a grand total of one female character but damn does she know what she's doing. And after the initial leaving her behind and "we should send her back" argument, there's no question about her not helping. She's a woman in a man's world, and she is helpful and wise while always still being a woman. <br>It's a great book, my kids love it, and there's a lot to work with.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14115269215765454518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2954637003" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2954637003" />
    <a title="Phillip Murrell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71546043-phillip-murrell"><img alt="Phillip Murrell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505660688p2/71546043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2954637003?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phillip Murrell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phillip Murrell" href="/user/show/71546043-phillip-murrell">Phillip Murrell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2954637003" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4866716476728612575">This book was amazing! I loved the movie, but as so often is the case, the book was far superior. I was surprised the Horned King didn't return. I associate him with the title, but he was really the villain from the first book. There were some differences, but they proved to be pleasant surprises. I look forward to reading the next book in the series and seeing how the more grown Taran and Eilowny deal with the threats of Arawn.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bZdJER5k+KnCZXjZDVHBd7wtq9B9c1pJTXxPJFDiSGTXZ2dQqs8DgWaaM3V03EWC+EKELlT7ypOT8zllcLgPVA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('h1uXEurJMzitn4w3e6sXdkliXfg5QbDhu7vh/uixlZ89q7lTXmLIEAlgx5sCJpODDQ1yBhDJIDtlNJe/yOvSrw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Excerpt: Talking to Dragons is a young adult fantasy novel, the fourth and final book in the Enchanted Forest Chronicles by Patricia Wrede. It is told in first person from the point of view of sixteen-year-old Daystar, son of Cimorene, a woman who lives at the edge of the Enchanted Forest. Cimorene raises Daystar and teaches him legends about the Enchanted forest, swordsmanship, spells, and magical protocols. One day, Antorell, a member of the Society of Wizards, who has a grudge against Cimorene tries to assault them. Then, Cimorene melts Antorell with a spell, which raises many questions in Daystar\'s mind because he didn\'t know that his mother could do any magic. However, Cimorene refuses to answer Daystar\'s questions, and goes into the Enchanted Forest to retrieve a sword, and gives it to Daystar. She then sends him into the forest telling him not to come back until he can &quot;tell her why he had to leave.&quot; When Daystar enters the forest, he meets a talking golden lizard named Suz, who tells Daystar that the sword Cimorene gave him is the Sword of the Sleeping King. Daystar, confused about what all this can mean, is instructed by Suz to &quot;follow the sword.&quot; Trying to find a place to spend the night, he enters the middle of a ring of hedges and finds a young fire witch named Shiara, who can sometimes do fire magic but can only do it periodically. The wizards heard about her lack of control and kidnapped her. However, she burned the Head Wizard\'s staff, ran away to the Enchanted Forest, and got caught in the middle of the hedges. Daystar tells Shiara about his quest, and she decides to accompany him.           <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/8924.Lloyd_Alexander">Lloyd Alexander
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
1,820
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16216938036659987009"><b>Lloyd Chudley Alexander</b> was an influential American author of more than forty books, mostly fantasy novels for children and adolescents, as well as several adult books. His most famous contribution to the field of children's literature is the fantasy series <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/40371-the-chronicles-of-prydain' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Chronicles of Prydain</a>. The concluding book of the series, <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24781.The_High_King' title='The High King' rel='nofollow noopener'>The High King</a>
</i>, was awarded the Newbery Medal in 1969. Alexander's other book</span>
  <span id="freeText16216938036659987009" style="display:none"><b>Lloyd Chudley Alexander</b> was an influential American author of more than forty books, mostly fantasy novels for children and adolescents, as well as several adult books. His most famous contribution to the field of children's literature is the fantasy series <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40371-the-chronicles-of-prydain" rel="nofollow noopener">The Chronicles of Prydain</a>. The concluding book of the series, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24781.The_High_King" title="The High King" rel="nofollow noopener">The High King</a>
</i>, was awarded the Newbery Medal in 1969. Alexander's other books have also won the National Book Award and the American Book Award. He was also one of the creators of <i>Cricket Magazine.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16216938036659987009" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
